# Dashboard PRD Plan: Fleet Surfaces

**Source:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/12-fleet-surfaces.md`
**Generated:** 2026-04-25
**Source hash:** `203d77f746e3f5b53aafdf432359bccb37c7549857074808dc43c926be7ebdb0`
**Section tasks:** 70
**Context mode:** full source section embedded in every task; no excerpt truncation.
**Quality threshold:** every task must score at least 9.5/10 before implementation begins.

## Purpose
Turn every dashboard PRD section into explicit backend-support work. Even visual/frontend sections must produce backend projection, telemetry, fixture, schema, or explicit no-backend rationale so frontend implementation is easy and stable.

## Global Implementation Rules
- Extend existing modules before creating new ones; only add new route/service files when no canonical owner exists.
- Implement production wiring, not only structs, mocks, or isolated helpers.
- Preserve every extracted detail unless a parity-ledger row explicitly marks it covered or deferred.
- Add persistence, events, auth/safety, dashboard projections, and docs updates whenever the requirement reaches those surfaces.
- A checked box means code, tests, docs, parity ledger, and strict gates are done for that task.

## Primary Target Areas
- `crates/roko-serve/src/routes/agents.rs`
- `crates/roko-serve/src/routes/templates.rs`
- `crates/roko-serve/src/routes/team.rs`
- `crates/roko-serve/src/routes/secrets.rs`

- Chain: default to devnet/simulation, prove contract/client/indexer sync, enforce wallet/risk/simulation gates, and record audit/witness data.
- Runtime: wire into the production agent loop with lifecycle, cancellation, health, audit, provider/tool safety, and observable events.
- Frontend support: provide stable projections, mock fixtures, empty/loading/stale/degraded/unauthorized states, and realtime update payloads that match projection schemas.
- Config/deployment: validate defaults, hot reload or restart-required paths, env var diagnostics, service dry-runs, and non-destructive operations.

### DASH-12-S002 -- Section overview

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/12-fleet-surfaces.md:7` through `22`
**Heading level:** H2
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `config-deployment`, `knowledge-learning`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
## Section overview

The Fleet section is the home of agents as first-class objects. Users come here to see their own agents, manage them, look at individual agents in detail, browse templates to spin up new ones, discover agents on the network, and coordinate groups of agents for shared work.

Fleet contains five pages: Agent Fleet, Agent Detail, Templates, Network, Groups.

- **Agent Fleet** — the user's owned agents as cards and tables. The primary management surface.
- **Agent Detail** — the canonical detail page for one agent, reached from anywhere an agent is clickable.
- **Templates** — preset agent configurations users can fork and deploy.
- **Network** — discovery surface for all registered agents on the chain.
- **Groups** — coordinated subsets of agents for shared work.

Fleet is where a Solo Operator lives day to day and where a Fleet Orchestrator spends most of their time. It is the operational heart of the product for users who primarily work with agents (vs arenas or knowledge).

---
````

````markdown
### Page structure

**Header area**: page title "Agent Fleet," block height, lens switcher if applicable. Right-aligned: a prominent "Create Agent" button opening Agent Composer (see `19-authoring-surfaces.md`).

**Section 01 — Agent Fleet.** Description: "Registered agents across all domains. Click any card to inspect, chat, or configure."

Content:

**View toggle** at top: Cards (default) / Table. Users can choose how the fleet is rendered.

**Search and filter bar**:
- Search input (by name, ID, capability keywords).
- Tier filter (All Tiers / Unverified / Basic / Verified / Trusted / Sovereign).
- Status filter (All Statuses / Running / Paused / Stuck / Failed).
- Additional actions: "Clear All" to reset filters, "Seed Fleet" for demo data (dev environments only), "Create Agent" as primary CTA.

**Fleet summary row**: "N AGENT(S), M ONLINE."

**Card view.** A responsive grid of agent cards. Each card shows:
- Generative agent portrait at top-left.
- Agent name as heading.
- Tier badge (with metal accent on card border).
- Model (mono label) and backend (e.g., "claude-sonnet-4-6 · claude_cli").
- A compact status row with: gate percentage, task count, reputation score.
- Recent activity indicator (pulse if active, muted if paused).
- Click a card → Agent Detail.

**Table view.** A dense table, one row per agent. Columns: portrait, name, domain, model, status, tier, tasks, gate %, cost, last active. Sortable by any column. Same data as card view, optimized for dense scanning.

**Section 02 — On-Chain Registry.** Description: "Agents registered directly on the Mirage devnet. Immutable records of identity and capability."

Content: a compact listing of the user's agents that have on-chain passports. Each entry shows:
- Agent ID (passport token ID, in mono).
- Registration block.
- Capabilities (as chips).
- Current reputation tier.
- A status indicator for "on-chain" vs "off-chain" (unregistered agents appear elsewhere).

This section bridges the off-chain Agent Fleet view with the on-chain reality. Registered agents appear in both; unregistered agents appear only in the main fleet view above.

**Section 03 — Agent Stats.** Description: "Performance metrics from the chain-extension intelligence layer."

Content: an aggregate stats table across the user's on-chain-registered agents. Columns: Agent ID, Insights, Tasks Done, Tasks Failed, Challenges, Confirms. Data pulled from ReputationRegistry and aggregate event logs.

Each row clickable to Agent Detail for that agent.
````

### Interactions

- Click a card or row → Agent Detail.
- Hover a card → larger preview popover (recent activity, more metrics).
- Right-click → context menu: Message, Pause, Resume, Delete, Fork, Publish as Template, View Passport.
- Bulk select via checkboxes → bulk actions: Pause All, Resume All, Delete Selected, Add to Group, Export Configs.
- Filter chips above the grid clear individually or via "Clear All."
- Switch between Cards and Table view persists per user.
````

### DASH-12-S019 -- Tab: Overview

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/12-fleet-surfaces.md:156` through `167`

#### Tab: Overview

**Vital signs panel**: at-a-glance state indicators. Current status (running/paused/stuck/terminal), uptime, current cognitive tier, heartbeat cadence, last tick timestamp.

**Recent activity panel**: a Timeline primitive showing heartbeat ticks, tool calls, gate results over the last hour. Users can zoom out to see longer history.

**Reputation panel**: a Tier Ladder showing the agent's current tier. Alongside: current reputation score per domain, trajectory indicators (rising, steady, declining), reputation history chart.

**Current workspace panel**: what the agent is "thinking about" right now. The current assembled context (high-level summary), current active task, current goals. This is a window into the agent's state.

**Recent outputs panel**: the last few outputs the agent produced (tool calls, knowledge entries, messages). A compact feed.
````

- Section word count: `123`
- Section hash: `3940f6664d7681cd20a235060dfd23effe45feca2a541760c5ba44b66a6c9bcc`

````markdown
#### Tab: Configuration

*Visible with full detail to owners. Public-only summary for non-owners.*

**Domain and extensions**: the agent's configured domain profile, the extensions it has loaded, the gates in its pipeline. Each listed as a chip with ability to inspect.

**Model routing**: which models the agent uses per cognitive tier, its cascade router state, cost preferences.

**Context policy**: how the agent assembles context — section priorities, token budgets, which knowledge sources it queries.

**Budgets**: daily/weekly/monthly cost caps. Current burn rate vs cap.

**Delegations**: what the agent is authorized to do (cryptoeconomic caveats). Reference to System → Delegations for full editing.

**Knowledge subscriptions**: which knowledge sources the agent draws from (chain-wide, specific authors, specific domains).

For owners: an "Edit" button on each section opens editing UI. For non-owners: all sections are read-only.
````

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
#### Tab: Knowledge

A scoped view of the agent's knowledge — entries it has produced, entries it has consumed, resonance patterns.

**Produced knowledge**: list of knowledge entries authored by this agent. Uses the Knowledge Store primitive, scoped.

**Consumed knowledge**: entries this agent has queried and applied successfully. Shows which entries were most useful in recent work.

**Resonance pattern**: a small Resonance Graph primitive showing the agent's knowledge neighborhood — where its output clusters in the HDC space.
````

### DASH-12-S022 -- Tab: Episodes

### DASH-12-S038 -- Interactions

**Source section:** `/Users/will/dev/nunchi/nunchi-dashboard/docs/prd/12-fleet-surfaces.md:339` through `345`
**Heading level:** H3
**Concern split:** `api`, `realtime`, `storage`, `chain`, `agent-runtime`, `dashboard-support`, `config-deployment`
**Implementation status:** `[ ] not started` `[ ] in progress` `[ ] implemented` `[ ] verified`

**Full source context for this task:**

````markdown
### Interactions

- Click "Deploy" on a template → opens Agent Composer with template pre-loaded as starting point.
- Click a template card → template detail view (read-only: full config, adoption stats, reviews, lineage).
- From template detail: Fork (to customize and optionally republish), Deploy (to spin up), or just study the config.
- Publish a fork: goes through a publish flow with rename, category selection, public/private toggle.
````

````markdown
### Page structure

**Header area**: page title "Network," block height, lens switcher. A search bar prominent.

**Section 01 — Network Registry.** Description: "Every agent on the chain. Browse, filter, discover."

Content:

**Search and filter bar**:
- Search by name, ID, capability, or owner.
- Domain filter.
- Tier filter.
- Capability filter (declared capabilities).
- Reputation sort.
- Activity sort (recent).

**Results**:
- Default view: grid of agent cards similar to Agent Fleet, scaled for density.
- Compact table view available.

Each card shows: portrait, name, tier badge, owner (truncated address), declared capabilities as chips, reputation per top domain, recent activity indicator.

**Section 02 — Featured Agents.** *(above the search results, curated)*

Content: cards for highlighted agents — newly-reached Sovereign tier, recently-published meta-agents, agents currently running notable public tasks. Curated by System Steward or algorithmically.

**Section 03 — Domain Leaders.** Description: "Top agents by reputation in each domain."

Content: a horizontal grouping by domain. For each domain (coding, DeFi, research, etc.), show the top N agents by reputation. A user can click through to see full rankings.
````

````markdown
### Page structure

**Header area**: page title "Groups," block height, lens switcher. Primary action: "Create Group."

**Section 01 — My Groups.** Description: "Coordinated agent collectives you own or participate in."

Content: a grid of group cards. Each card:
- Group name.
- Purpose / description line.
- Member count and member portraits (top 4–6 visible).
- Coordination protocol indicator (role-based, market-based, hierarchical, emergent).
- Activity level indicator (active, idle, paused).
- Ownership indicator (owner / member / observer).

**Section 02 — Active Coordination.** Description: "Current activity across your groups."

Content: a feed showing recent notable events across the user's groups: a group completed a shared task, a group admitted a new member, a group resolved a conflict, a group published a shared knowledge entry.

**Section 03 — Public Groups.** *(visible when lens is Global)*

Content: public groups available to join. Each card shows the group's purpose, membership criteria, and an apply/join action.
````

- Config/deployment: validate defaults, hot reload or restart-required paths, env var diagnostics, service dry-runs, and non-destructive operations.

### Bulk operation safety

Bulk operations (bulk pause, bulk delete) always require explicit confirmation with a clear summary of what will happen. "Delete 37 agents? This cannot be undone." Dangerous bulk operations have extra safeguards.
